Protecting Traffic on the Hunan-Hubei Railway

Changsha Correspondence: In the recent two months, train traffic from Changsha to Wuchang has been intermittent. The railway stations, sleepers, and roadbed bridges of the Luojiang, Taolin, Huangshajie, Matang, Yingjiawan, Guiyi, and Yunxi stations between Yuezhou and Xiangyin have been burned and destroyed by bandits. Wherever the bandits went, they ordered the residents along the road to send a hoe from each family (men must hold iron hoes to register with the bandits, and women must also send one person if there are no men) and take on the task of destroying the railway, or the whole family would be burned and killed. Therefore, the losses and material consumption of the Hunan-Hubei Road this time have been unprecedented in previous military operations. Moreover, the repair and damage have been carried out in a rotational manner for nearly two months. The military and road workers are exhausted, and the impact on military affairs and commerce is significant. Initially, Qian Dajun's Teaching Division was responsible for the suppression, and then a part of Wang Dongyuan's 15th Division was added to assist. Recently, the entire 31st Division of Tao Guang was added, suppressing from different routes. The bandits, including Kong Helong, Li Hangshi, Hu Yun (female bandit), and Hou Qi, were driven east of the railway line and fled towards Pingjiang. Now, the headquarters of the Fourth Route Army, in addition to ordering Tao Guang's entire division and Hou Pengfei's brigade of Wang Dongyuan's division, as well as Zhu Xingshu's bandit suppression detachment, to form a large encirclement to suppress Pingjiang, is still worried that there are still remaining bandits lurking, disturbing the rear, and destroying the railway tracks again. Therefore, the Second Brigade of Tong Kun's troops of the Xiangxi Bandit Suppression Command and the two regiments of the headquarters' Independent Regiment Ye Wenke's troops, as well as Guo Bugao's Second Bandit Suppression Detachment, have been dispatched to various stations in the Chang-Yue section to be responsible for maintaining railway and telegraph line traffic and suppressing nearby scattered bandits, in order to ensure thoroughness. The order of the headquarters of the Fourth Route Army is recorded as follows: (It is found that the Wu-Chang Railway is related to the traffic between Hunan and Hubei, and troops should be stationed at key points to maintain the road administration. It is ordered that the troops of Brigade Commander Tong Kun of the Second Brigade of the Xiangxi Bandit Suppression Command be stationed in the Luojiang Xinshi Guiyi area, and also take into account the defense of Baishui Taolin. The troops of Regiment Commander Ye Wenke of the Independent Regiment shall take a train from Changsha to Huangshajie immediately, taking into account Yingjiawan, and closely liaising with Tong's troops in Taolin Temple. The troops of the Second Bandit Suppression Detachment Commander Guo Bugao shall take a train from Changsha to Yunxi immediately, taking into account the defense of Lukou Chenglingji, and closely liaising with Tao's (Guang) troops in Yuezhou. Each of these troops shall be fully responsible for the designated stationed and taken-care sections, and completely eliminate the nearby scattered bandits. If there is any negligence, severe punishment will be given.) (October 20)

Fighting Near Nanning

Fierce Battle Lasted a Day and Night, Guangxi Army Retreats

Guangzhou dispatch: Fighting recently broke out near Nanning, Guangxi, and is currently still ongoing. The Guangxi army within the city of Nanning has long been surrounded by the Yunnan army. Therefore, Bai Chongxi's army from Liuzhou urgently wants to lift the siege of Yongguan, so that the troops of Huang Xuchu and Wei Yunsong in the city can escape danger. Bai has recently incorporated the old troops of Li Mingrui in the Longzhou area, to contain the rear of the 10th Route Yunnan Army led by Lu Han. Bai Chongxi then led his newly formed troops out of Longshan and Wuming, to contain the 8th Route Army led by Yu Hanmou stationed in Binyang. On the 11th of this month, they suddenly launched attacks on the defense areas of the 8th and 10th Routes in three directions, with about 3,000 to 4,000 troops. Bai Chongxi's troops advanced from Wuming, Zhen Hedong's troops came out of Shanglin Silong, and Li Mingrui's troops attacked the rear of the Yunnan army at Fufeng from Chongshan. At the same time, the Guangxi army under Huang Xuchu and Wei Yunsong in Yongcheng also broke out of the siege, launching counterattacks against the 8th and 10th Route Armies in different directions. The Guangxi army from Silong advanced to the Goulou Pass, confronting the brigade of Li Zhenqiu of Yu Fu's division of the 8th Route Army. From the morning of the 12th to 4 p.m., the Guangxi army led by He was unsuccessful and began to retreat towards Longshan. According to the aircraft report on the 14th, our army (8th Route) Yu's Division, Li Zhenqiu's brigade, fought fiercely with the enemy near Goulou Pass in Silong at noon on the 12th. By Shenshi (3-5 p.m.), He Zhendong's enemy was defeated. In this battle, more than 500 enemies were killed, more than four water-cooled machine guns, three mortars, and more than 300 rifles were seized, and more than 400 prisoners were captured. Our army suffered 30 to 40 casualties, and is currently still in pursuit. Our aircraft are conducting reconnaissance and bombing every day, killing many enemies. [Signed] Zhang Zixuan. The 8th Route Commander-in-Chief Chen Jitang arrived in Wuzhou at 4 p.m. on the 15th, and will inspect the Wuzhou troops before departing for Dahe, Pingnan, and other places to inspect defense. As for Shanglin (90 li from Binyang) in the front, it is located at the border of Binyang and Wuming. Li's Brigade of Yu Hanmou's Division has already advanced to Shanglin to concentrate. The two departments of the teaching brigade, Zeng Youren and Zhang Zhiying, were sent to Binyang to take over the defense, and Fan Dexing and Chen Hanguang's two regiments were stationed to guard Qianjiang and Litang. It is heard that the enemy has also been increasing troops to Wuming, Qianjiang, and Shanglin for days. There will probably still be a major battle near Binyang. To the southwest of Nanning, on the 12th, battles also broke out simultaneously with Silong and Shanglin. On that day, a part of the Guangxi army came out of Wuming and fought fiercely for several hours with the 98th Division Sun Du brigade of the 10th Route Yunnan Army and the 99th Division Zhu Xu's Zeng Shuhuai brigade stationed on Gaofeng Ridge in northern Yong. According to Lu Han's report on the 12th, the enemy launched an attack on the 10th regiment stationed at Gaofeng, and we responded, breaking through the enemy's formation, capturing two water-cooled machine guns, hundreds of rifles, and banners, symbols, rosters, and other items. Many others were captured and killed. Troops are still being sent to pursue. [Signed] Lu Han. It was found that on the 12th, the Yunnan army responded in two directions. The two troops of Wei Yunsong and Lei of the Guangxi army rushing out of Yongcheng were repulsed by the two divisions of the Yunnan army Zhu Xu and Zhang Chong in the Shaping Wushui River area in southern Yong. The Guangxi army Li Mingrui's troops that attacked from Taiping Prefecture were resisted by Lu Han who personally led his troops. The two sides fought fiercely for a day and night, and the Wei and Li enemy troops were defeated. Now the two troops of Wei and Lei have retreated back to Yongcheng, while Li Mingrui's troops have retreated back to Longzhou. (October 17)

Partial Opening of Traffic Between Tianjin and Jinan

Jinan dispatch: Recently, the No. 90-2 freight and passenger mixed train between Tianjin and Jinan originally took Dezhou as the boundary. Only the locomotives were exchanged in Dezhou, and other freight and passenger mixed trains did not need to be changed. The passenger and freight tickets were also through tickets from Tianjin to Jinan. However, the revenue north of Dezhou belonged to the Tianjin Bureau, and the revenue south of Dezhou belonged to the Pukou Bureau. However, starting today, there has been another change. Jinan Station received an order from the Pukou Bureau that from the 20th, the No. 10 train departing from Jinan North will stop at Dezhou and will no longer go north. In Dezhou, it will be changed to No. 9 train and return. At night, it will be changed to No. 12 to Dezhou, and in Dezhou it will be changed to No. 11 train to return. Jinan Station sells tickets to Dezhou. Passengers and goods going north from Dezhou must buy separate tickets. Free tickets south of Dezhou are not valid. Tianjin Station sells tickets to Dezhou. Passengers and goods going south from Dezhou must also buy separate tickets. Free tickets are also not valid south of Dezhou. Both passenger and freight transport feel inconvenienced by this. However, the reason for this is that both railway bureaus are cautious about the vehicles, and there are no other problems. The arrival times of each train between Jinan and Dezhou are recorded as follows: Train No. 10 from Jinan to Dezhou departs at 11 a.m. and arrives in Dezhou at 2:54 p.m. At 5 p.m., it is changed to No. 9 and departs from Dezhou, arriving in Jinan at 9:06 p.m. At 12 a.m., it is changed back to Train No. 12 and departs from Jinan to Dezhou, arriving in Dezhou at 3:54 a.m. the next morning. At 6 a.m., it is changed to No. 11 and departs from Dezhou, arriving in Jinan at 10:06 a.m. At 11 a.m., it is changed back to No. 10 and returns. In short, it is just this one train that travels back and forth between Dezhou and Jinan. (October 20)

Post-War Inspection Notes on the Longhai Railway

Recent Situation in Zhengzhou

Zhengzhou dispatch: A reporter group from Xuzhou inspected Zhengzhou, and the following is a record of what they saw and heard.

Recent Situation in Zhengbu: The reporter group left Bianxi at 7 p.m. on the 15th and passed through Hanzhuang, Zhongmu, Baisha, Gucheng, etc. along the way. No war trenches were found. However, there was a lot of white sand, and the sand on both sides of the railway was half a foot thick, which was very desolate. At 11 p.m., they arrived at Zhengzhou Railway Station. At that time, the rear troops of the Central Army were waiting to be demobilized and boarded the train from Zhengzhou. All the inns were full and there was no room to stand. The reporter group temporarily rested at the Zhengzhou Office of the Longhai Transportation Command. According to Deputy Director You Fei, traffic between Zhengzhou and Luoyang was restored on the 12th, and through tickets were available from the 14th, with one train running every day. The westbound train can now reach Shaanxi. The Yellow River Bridge on the Pinghan Railway was damaged when Feng's army retreated, but it has now been repaired. The northbound train can reach the southern end of the Yellow River Bridge. The next morning, they inspected the commercial port and found cellars everywhere. The four cellars under the platform were very large, dozens of steps in size, covered with earth and zhangs (unit of measurement, roughly 3 meters). It was said that they were inhabited by senior generals of Feng's army. Feng stayed in Zhengzhou more often during the war. At first, he lived in Fushou Street in the commercial port, but due to the fierce attacks by the Central Air Force, he moved to the Chenghuang Temple in the city. The National Hotel, Fuchang Hotel, and Wuzhou Hotel in the commercial port where his senior generals lived were all bombed by planes. At 10 p.m. on the 6th, Feng's army went west. Hao Mengling's 54th Division of the Central Army was the first to enter the city port. Hao was appointed Zhengzhou Garrison Commander. Since a large number of troops are gathered at the moment, they are waiting to be demobilized, and post-war matters are still being handled. At noon, they went to Zhengxian County to inspect the city, which is located two li northeast of the station. The bricks and stones have been removed, leaving only the earth foundation. The earth foundations around the city are all dug with cellars, arranged like honeycombs. The houses in the city also have cellars. County Magistrate Xie Zechao has only been in office for three days. The county government only has 60 guard guns. When Feng's army was in the countryside, they established a military service committee to supply everything. The committee is still continuing to operate. Various losses are still under investigation. The city is extremely desolate, fully displaying the post-war scene.

Military Interview: On the 16th, the command was visited. The command is located behind the ticket office of the station. Director He arrived in Zhengzhou from Wuhan on the 12th, and the command has just been established. Since He was busy with official duties, he was received by Chief of Staff Zhou Weigang. According to reports, the current military situation is that Feng's army retreated to Hebei. The troops of Sun Liangcheng, Sun Lianzhong, Sun Dianying, Liu Ruming, and Pang Bingxun have mostly contacted the central government to express their sincerity. The central government has always been generous and has not yet crossed the river to pursue them. Those who retreated to the west were the troops of Song Zheyuan and Ge Yunlong, etc., who have now retreated to the pass. The central government's pursuit team has already passed Shaanxi. As for the troops of Ji Hongchang, who have surrendered, they will be transferred to Xiangcheng for reorganization. Liang Guanying's troops will also be transferred from Ronggong back to Dezhou for reorganization. The military post-war matters in Henan Province are nothing more than relieving suffering and recuperating. They are currently reporting to the central government for handling. In the afternoon, Garrison Commander Hao Mengling was visited again. The garrison headquarters is located in Hefeng Inn in the commercial port. It is understood that Hao's 54th Division and Shangguan Yunxiang's 47th Division were organized into the Third Column when they attacked from the Pinghan Railway. They advanced on the west side of the route and attacked Zhengzhou between Xuchang and Yuzhou. The 47th Division moved into the Xushui Town south of the Longhai Railway, cutting off the Longhai Railway. Hao's Division directly took Zhengzhou, fighting fiercely with Feng's army in the Huanggang Temple and Shili Pu area southwest of Zhengzhou. Feng's army dug gathering point trenches around Zhengzhou, which were dug in the recent month. After breaking through the battlements, they entered Zhengzhou on the evening of the 6th. At that time, Xinzheng and Changge had not yet fallen. The Feng's army combat troops along the way were a small part of the Jin army in Yingqiao west of Xu, Ruan Xuanwu's troops in Yuzhou, and Feng's army purely in the suburbs of Zhengzhou. There were fierce battles in Meizishan, Wangkou, and other places, and about a dozen large cannons were captured. Hao was commissioned on the 8th and his troops were responsible for the defense of Zhengzhou. The 47th Division was also stationed in Zhengzhou for temporary rest.

Disaster Statistics: Zhengzhou was the rear base of Feng's army's Longping routes during the war. It was the most requisitioned and suffered the most. Since Feng's army came east, Zhengxian County was ordered to establish a military service committee, with the seven district chiefs of the county responsible. The commercial port was the responsibility of the Chamber of Commerce. According to the statistics of the military service committee, the committee handled about 1,000 large carts, with an average of three animals and two laborers per cart, and more than 1,000 stretcher bearers. 4,000 soldiers were conscripted. Almost all men between the ages of 15 and 60 were enlisted. The trenches around the city were all dug by civilians, with two meals a day. The length of the trenches was about 30 li from east to west and about 20 li from north to south, surrounding the east, south, west, and one corner of the northwest. Most of the villages were used as trenches for concealment. There were communication trenches between the villages to connect them. The excavation took

Page 7

Domestic News Roundup

more than two weeks. The closest was five li from the city, and the farthest was about 20 li, occupying more than 20 villages. The trenches stretched for more than 100 li. A total of 1.1 million jin of wheat, more than 800,000 jin of millet, more than 2 million jin of bran, 9 million jin of firewood, and 7 million jin of horse grass were requisitioned. The Northwest Bank's non-redeemable "added-character tickets" were used to exchange for cash, amounting to 40,000 yuan. The so-called "added-character tickets" were tickets originally printed by the Northwest Bank with added characters printed on the back. All these supplies were borne by the farmers, with each mu (unit of area) charged more than two yuan. However, the above statistics are only those handled by the committee. It is estimated that the free requisition in the countryside is more than ten or a hundred times that amount. The Finance Department of Feng's army requisitioned 7,000 yuan from the county every month. The expenses handled by the military service committee were more than one million yuan. According to the statistics of the Chamber of Commerce, Feng's army needed 30,000 jin of flour and 20,000 jin of millet every day when they were in Zhengzhou. Since entering Zhengzhou, they demanded this amount every day. At first, they used opium as payment. The military station distributed opium twice. The first time was 8,590 taels, and the second time was 28,200 taels, with an average price of two yuan per tael. Later, they used requisitioned wheat as exchange, which was handled by Tongyi Gong Flour Mill. When Weishou Commander Li Guanglong was in Zhengzhou, he demanded 2,000 yuan per month to cover expenses. When retreating, he demanded 30,000 sets of overcoats from Zhengbu. They did not have time to make them all, so they ordered 10,000 sets to be made in Zhengzhou and 10,000 sets in Xinxiang. Later, due to the hasty retreat, they changed it to 100,000 yuan, then to 60,000 yuan and 30,000 yuan, and finally took 20,000 yuan away. During the war, about 200 people were killed and about 500-600 people were injured in the entire port. The losses of houses and property are still under investigation. When Feng's army was in Zhengzhou last year, the discipline was very good. This time, the hungry army's discipline was disrupted, and it was even more chaotic during the retreat. Whenever they encountered someone with neat clothes and hats, they would borrow money from them to cover their travel expenses. According to Zhengzhou people, the market in the commercial port may be restored next year due to the convenience of transportation. The countryside was severely affected by the disaster, and nine out of ten houses were empty. Furthermore, due to the lack of livestock and vehicles, it is difficult to sow wheat, and there is no hope for the spring harvest. It is feared that it will not be restored for four or five years. This year's winter is cold, and next year's spring famine is even more worrying. Relief efforts cannot be delayed. (October 17)

A Glimpse of Bandits in Dingyuan, Northern Anhui

A Large Group of Ferocious Bandits Broke in at Dawn

Entrenched for a Day, Retreated Only at Night

Bengbu dispatch: Dingyuan is a small town in northern Anhui, with a closed atmosphere and fierce customs. In recent years, due to the impact of war, bandits have appeared in the territory from time to time, but fortunately there are no large gangs of bandits, so the harm is not too severe. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 15th of this month, suddenly seven or eight hundred ferocious bandits sneaked to the outside of the county seat, hoping to rob the county seat. The next day (16th) at dawn, as soon as the city gate opened, the bandits suddenly broke in through the north gate, half with red spears and half with quick guns, very fierce. They seized the guns of the city gate guards, and divided into two groups to enter the city. One group rushed directly to the district security group, the finance bureau, and the prison, confiscating the firearms of the security group, then looting the finance bureau, driving away the staff of the prison, and releasing the prisoners. The other group besieged the county government and attacked to the outside of the signature room. County Magistrate Xu Yongxiu hurriedly led the county government soldiers to bravely attack. Gunfire in the office was boiling. County Magistrate Xu supervised the team and fought fiercely with the bandits for more than an hour, and then drove the bandits out of the county government gate, killing four bandits on the spot and capturing one alive. The bandits then increased their large team and surrounded the county government on three sides, launching fierce attacks. The police team in the county government also bravely resisted, so the bandits failed to attack. Soon the local militia outside the city heard the alarm and quickly joined hundreds of people to enter the city and attack from both sides. Most of the bandits were driven out of the city, but there were still more than 200 people who were entrenched in the security group, the finance bureau, and the prison, stubbornly resisting. County Magistrate Xu led the team to surround them on three sides, and fought fiercely for another five hours. Just as the temporarily organized 3rd Regiment of the 45th Division passed through the territory and attacked from inside and outside, the bandits could not support themselves and broke out from the south gate in the evening, fleeing. About a dozen bandits were killed, and the people also suffered slight casualties. Zhang Daocun, a staff member of the county government, was injured in the foot. The land tax collection office, tax deed office, dispatch office, and urban slaughter office were all looted. The number of shops and households that were robbed was also not small, and the local losses were quite large. (October 20)

Tobacco Seedlings Widely Planted in Various Counties in Southern Fujian

Provincial Government Strictly Orders Fang Shengtao and Zhang Zhen to Investigate and Prohibit

Fuzhou dispatch: Since the military uprising, the ban on tobacco in southern Fujian has gradually become lax again, and unscrupulous soldiers have even sheltered it. It is heard that Yang Shuzhuang has now immediately telegraphed military commissioners Fang Shengtao and Zhang Zhen, the commander of the Xin Yi Division, to be responsible for the investigation and prohibition, and ordered the armies under their command not to knowingly violate the prohibition. The reason is that in the Tongyanping Pacification Office, there are instances of condoning the private planting of tobacco seedlings by villagers, levying donations on cultivated land, and sheltering the planting of opium poppies on their behalf. The price has risen from more than 20 yuan to more than 100 yuan, so it is necessary to strictly prohibit it.

Furthermore, the people of Quanzhou recently filed a complaint against Fang Shengtao for various inappropriate measures, requesting the abolition of the Military Commissioner's Office. They also said that the Military Commissioner's Office actually hinted to the stationed army to persuade the people to plant tobacco seedlings. Now Jinjiang, Nan'an, Hui'an, Tongan, and Yongchun counties have successively planted them, hoping to collect a large amount of tobacco donations. It is also said that the tobacco donation in Tongan County has been set at one million yuan. However, it is unknown how the government will deal with it. (October 17)

Chairman of Hebei Province Wang Shuchang Sworn In

Tianjin dispatch: Wang Shuchang, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, held a supplementary oath of office ceremony at 10 a.m. on the 17th. Wu Tiecheng was sent by the central government as a representative to Tianjin to supervise the oath. Wu arrived in Tianjin from Shenyang on the morning of the 15th. Today (17th), merchants and residents throughout the city hung flags. Armed posts were added to Dahu Tong and Tianjin Road by the 25th Brigade, presenting a solemn atmosphere. Party and national flags were hung at the gates of the provincial government. In the center of the auditorium hung the portrait and will of the Prime Minister. In front of the ceremonial table were the seats for the chairman and the oath supervisor. The seats for military police were on the left, and the seats for news reporters and various legal groups were on the right. Behind the chairman were the seats for the heads of various departments and the leaders of various institutions. Further behind were the seats for ordinary guests, totaling more than 300 people. Although the heads of the various departments of the provincial government have already taken office, they were not convenient to take the oath with Wang at the same time because they have not yet received appointments from the National Government, and only participated in the ceremony. The one who came to Tianjin by train last night was the Director of Civil Affairs Wang Yuke. The other Director of Finance Yao Hong, Director of Construction Lin Chengxiu, Director of Agriculture and Mining Chang Bingyi, Director of Industry and Commerce He Yufang, and Director of Education Zhang Jian'an all arrived in Tianjin by the early train today. Zhang Xueliang's representative Zhao Ti arrived at 9:20 a.m. Central representative Wu Tiecheng also arrived at 10:10 a.m. and was led to the back building to rest by Chief Receptionist Liu Yunhong. At 10:40 a.m., the guests gathered in the auditorium. After the opening ceremony, Wang Shuchang raised his left hand to take the oath. Next, central representative Wu Tiecheng delivered a speech, roughly stating that today Chairman Wang is taking a supplementary oath. Tiecheng was ordered by Chairman Jiang of the National Government to supervise the oath, and it is a great honor to participate in the grand ceremony. Hebei has suffered from the tyrannical rule of warlords for three years. Yan Xishan recklessly used the remnants of feudalism, disregarded the people, and treated Hebei as a vassal state, taking the wealth of Hebei as an external treasury, levying taxes and grabbing, exhausting the people, and the market was in decline, and the people hated it. The central government felt sorry for the local area, and ordered the troops of the Northeast to enter the customs to fight against the rebels, relieving the people's plight. The rebel party has collapsed, and the people must be actively pacified. Therefore, Chairman Wang was appointed to govern the province, eliminate the tyranny, and reduce the harsh taxes, taking the people out of the water and fire and putting them on the mat, and then implementing the party's doctrine, seeking local construction, promoting autonomy, and gradually reaching the era of constitutional government, so that the people can enjoy peace and happiness. It is not only the fortune of Hebei Province, but also the fortune of the country. I hope that the chairman will work hard to live up to the high expectations of the central government. After Wu finished his speech, Zhao delivered a speech, roughly stating that after the military destruction in Hebei Province, all construction must be carried out in a practical manner. Chairman Wang is knowledgeable and has extensive experience. He will certainly follow the Prime Minister's will, abide by national laws and the Three Principles of the People, not fail the country's trust, and create happiness for the Central Plains. I am here to participate in the ceremony, not only to congratulate Hebei Province on gaining talent, but also to congratulate the future of China. After Zhao finished his speech, Wang delivered a reply, saying that Shuchang was ordered to be the chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, and was encouraged by Mr. Wu Tiecheng, the oath supervisor of the National Government, and General Zhao, the representative of the deputy commander. Shuchang has served in the military and has no experience in politics. He can only follow the instructions, act according to his conscience, and do his best. Moreover, after the military ravages in Hebei Province, everything is waiting to be sorted out. Shuchang is mediocre, but he will do his best. I hope that all the guests will give guidance from time to time. After Wang finished his reply, Wu Tiecheng led the entire audience to shout "Long live the Republic of China" and "Long live Hebei Province", and then took photos and dispersed. (October 17)

Baker's Handling of Northwest Relief Efforts

Baker, advisor to the Ministry of Railways, was previously dispatched in February to assist with the China International Famine Relief Commission's relief efforts. He has now returned to Beijing. Regarding the progress of relief efforts in the Northwest provinces, he has prepared a detailed report and submitted it to Minister Sun for review. The following is a transcription of the report:

(Respectful submission to Minister Zhesheng: On February 11th of this year, I was dispatched to Ping (Beijing) to assist with the China International Famine Relief Commission's special relief efforts. The original leave was limited to June, but as matters were not yet completed, it was extended by another month. Now, I respectfully present to you a detailed account of the matters handled and the facts of the progress. When I arrived in Ping and took office as the Director of Relief Efforts for the commission, there was an available fund of 300,000 yuan for relief. The American side hoped for further assistance, as they were still raising funds in the United States, and the fundraising was still in progress. Under these circumstances, the relief plan adopted was largely the same as before. The disaster areas to be aided included Gansu, Shaanxi, Henan, and scattered areas in Shanxi and Shandong provinces. Suiyuan was also a disaster area, but irrigation projects were underway, and some parts had already been completed. With work as relief, the disaster situation could be slightly alleviated. The person in charge of Suiyuan's relief efforts was Mr. Shi Dejun, Mr. J. O. Toad. In Gansu, Reverend Ren Findlay Andrew was in charge. For scattered disaster areas, funds were remitted to local churches for distribution. The disaster situation in Shaanxi was relatively serious, so a branch was specially established in the province to manage and distribute the relief funds. The most difficult province to carry out relief efforts was Henan, where the political situation was extremely chaotic. Although relief was needed, no one was willing to come forward and take responsibility. At that time, the commission had over 600 tons of grain in storage, with about 700 tons more ordered but not yet arrived. The commission originally planned to purchase another 500 tons of mung beans from southern Shanxi and transport them to the disaster areas in Shaanxi by handcart and boat. However, due to problems with the transportation of the aforementioned 1,300 tons of grain, the plan was abandoned. This was because traffic on both the Pinghan and Longhai railways had been suspended. Under these circumstances, the only option was to transport the grain by rail to central Shanxi, then transfer it to trucks for transport south to the Yellow River, and then reload it onto boats for transport to the distribution points. However, after carefully inspecting the truck routes I passed, I realized that before the rainy season, the roads were still in good condition, and about 400 tons could be transported. If more needed to be transported, a large sum of money would have to be spent on purchasing vehicles, and there was no other way. With such delays, how could it be done? I therefore met with representatives from both Feng and Tu's sides, and informed them of the difficulties in relief efforts, requesting that they allow one or two relief cars to be attached to the military trains heading to Shaanxi each day. After several discussions, they agreed to open a special train to transport 500 tons. Seeing that the command of the various armies was not uniform, I also visited military and transportation officials in various places to request cooperation, and spent a great deal of time traveling back and forth. The grain purchased by the commission from the three northeastern provinces, after being transported to Fengtai, had an empty train car delivered to the commission for loading about every two days. A total of 2,000 tons of relief grain was transported to Shishi, the Yellow River terminus of the Hai route. With transportation no longer a problem, the commission contacted Buddhist charitable organizations familiar with relief efforts, and they established five porridge kitchens in western Henan to distribute 117 tons of grain to provide relief. With this effective means of transportation, we accepted as much grain as possible from various charities to transport to the disaster areas. The commission had only purchased a total of 1,300 tons of grain, but 2,000 tons of relief grain was transported to Shishi. The excess 700 tons were from these charitable donations. When the political situation in Shaanxi was extremely chaotic, the Xi'an branch advocated for remitting funds instead of transporting grain, but the grain had already been shipped, and it was impossible to stop. I believed that transporting grain was more appropriate than remitting funds, as it could reduce risks. Subsequent events proved this to be correct, as remittances without guarantees were not a prudent approach. I, seeing the inadequacy of the Xi'an branch in coping with the situation, sought out several people with organizational experience and a deep understanding of China to go to Xi'an to assist or even take charge of matters. Although three people were found, their qualifications were suitable, but it took a great deal of effort. This was because all workers in Shaanxi were regarded as bandits, and the epidemic was raging, so no one dared to try. I accompanied the three hired individuals to Xi'an. After the tasks were assigned, I returned to Beiping to handle various relief matters and resolve the issue of transporting grain to Shaanxi. However, the three previously sent individuals suddenly panicked and refused to stay. This was because banditry was rampant and the epidemic was widespread. One of the three soon resigned, and the other two also left. I had no choice but to personally go to Xi'an to handle relief matters. This was on July 4th of this year. At that time, the Feng army's battle zone had been reduced to a very short range, with a total front line of only 40 miles. Extreme protection was provided for the traffic from Tongguan to Luoyang, and then extended to a point about 50 miles away from Xi'an. In that area, rogue troops were extremely rampant, and merchants along the road were robbed daily, often threatening to cut off traffic to Tongguan. The people of Xi'an called these righteous troops "bandits," but they called themselves "righteous troops." Because travelers were repeatedly robbed by these troops, they had to travel in convoys of cars, escorted by soldiers. Soldiers were in the front and rear of the convoy, providing very tight protection, which reduced the danger somewhat. However, this method was not always reliable, and convoys were often turned back. Later, Liu Yufen ordered the county magistrates of various counties to summon the Red Spears Society and local militias to provide protection, and the banditry subsided. I and my staff, fearing that the relief supplies would also be robbed, went to see the leaders of the righteous troops (who were then in Xingping, which was besieged). The leaders expressed sympathy for the relief efforts and were willing to help, so they sent many guards to escort the supplies, allowing them to reach Xingping and the western disaster areas safely. The Feng army did not prevent this, which was fortunate. We originally intended to organize work teams to provide work as relief, so that the heads of households could earn wages to support their families. At the beginning of the organization, young farmers dared not join, as they were afraid of being forced into military service. However, both the Feng army and the anti-Feng army prohibited organized work teams from crossing their borders. We had no choice but to stop work in easily detected locations and instead focus on construction near the workers' homes. The construction plan at that time was to first improve the road from Xi'an to Tongguan, then to dredge ditches, and then to improve the highway from Xi'an west to the Gansu border. On the above roads, there were many streams, and the slopes varied from 12% to 30%. These slopes have now been uniformly reduced to 7%. In addition, several bridges were repaired, several river embankments were paved, and 5,000 miles of highways were added. The above projects should have been completed one after another by now. A few days before leaving Xi'an, I went with hydraulic engineer Mr. Ellison and several Chinese engineers and government officials to observe the site of a former irrigation structure built during the Three Kingdoms period. Some people have proposed tunneling through the mountain and building a sluice gate across the Jing River, so that the fields of Jingyang, Sanyuan, and Gaoling counties would be fully irrigated and free from drought and flood. However, later generations have argued about this, and no consensus has been reached. According to our observations, tunneling through the mountain would require a huge amount of money, which is beyond the current or recent financial situation. A compromise solution would be to build a dam on the river and enlarge the waterway rebuilt 300 years ago, and build several branch streams, so that the water storage capacity could irrigate at least 100,000 acres of farmland. A survey team has now been sent to investigate, and materials for this project have been ordered. The recruitment of workers is probably underway. The total cost of the project is estimated to be about 750,000 yuan, or perhaps more. The China International Famine Relief Commission currently has 350,000 yuan in funds. The commission intends to use this money for this project, which is the intention of the commission members. Relief funds will continue to arrive, so that the project can be completed. Many charitable organizations support the commission. For example, the North China Famine Relief Commission has allocated a large amount of relief funds to the commission for the construction of highways. That commission still has 200,000 yuan in relief funds. The total amount of the two commissions is not enough for this project, and it is also a huge difference from the Shaanxi relief funds for this winter. Therefore, alternative solutions must be found. Last year, there were 42 disaster areas in Shaanxi. Among them, 30 have had a very good harvest this year, which is a fact. However, the remaining 12 are located in the foothills of low-lying areas, and their plight is actually worse than last year. Although there has been a large amount of rainfall in the Wei River area, there has been very little rainfall from the first mountain range to the north of the Wei River. On August 1st of this year, locusts caused further damage, increasing the affected area by 20 miles. In total, the length is probably no less than 200 miles. The previous population of these 12 disaster areas was about 2 million, but now there are only 900,000. If no relief is provided, after winter, there will inevitably be another 600,000 deaths. The residents of the area are displaced and in extreme distress. Three-quarters of the residents' houses have been destroyed.

There is not a single tile left, and the wood has been sold off. Every day, 300 to 400 handcarts are loaded with this wood and sold in Xi'an. Another group of residents are selling all their household items to pay for their migration to find more fertile land. As for how to feed the aforementioned 600,000 disaster victims, maintaining them until the next harvest will take a long time and cost a lot. If each person is given 12 ounces of grain per day, the cost will be about 7 to 8 million yuan. The only solution now is to provide work as relief, so that the money is not wasted and both water conservancy and highways can be developed. If more mountain roads can be built, the province's coal mines can be developed, creating wealth (the current price of coal in Xi'an is about 67 yuan per ton). With commercial prosperity, the four classes of people will not suffer from unemployment, bandits will have no way to arise, and local order will be easily restored. I sincerely hope that you will convey the disaster situation in various places and the suffering of the people to the relief authorities, and ask them to work with all charitable organizations to seek relief. The current situation in the province is very different from the summer. Many highways have been expanded, and water conservancy has been improved, so it is no longer as lifeless as before. The commission's goods lost due to banditry amount to several hundred yuan in cash, six bags of beans, and vehicles that were robbed three times. The drivers' clothing and money were all taken away. However, vehicles escorted by Westerners have never been intercepted. I carried 50,000 yuan in cash, and although it passed through areas occupied by bandits, it was not robbed, which was fortunate. The amount spent by me this time totaled 1.25 million yuan, of which 600,000 yuan was used in Shaanxi, 500,000 yuan in Gansu, 100,000 yuan in Henan, and the remainder was used in smaller disaster areas scattered throughout the region. The commission's work teams were never forced into military service, nor did anyone die from the epidemic. This is a general overview of my handling of relief efforts.)

Political Program of the Chinese Nationalist Party

The Chinese Nationalist Party leads the National Revolution to seek freedom and equality for China.

··········

The Nationalism of the Nationalist Party has two meanings: first, the Chinese nation seeks its own liberation; second, all ethnic groups within China are equal.

···········

The Nationalist Party's Democracy advocates direct democracy (the rights of initiative, referendum, recall, and impeachment) in addition to indirect democracy.

···········

The Nationalist Party's Livelihood Principles have two main principles: first, equal land ownership; second, regulation of capital.

···········

Foreign Policy, Article 1: Any country that voluntarily renounces all privileges and is willing to abolish treaties that undermine China's sovereignty will be recognized by China as a most-favored nation.

···········

Domestic Policy, Article 2: Counties are designated as autonomous units. The people of autonomous counties have the right to directly elect and recall officials, and the right to directly initiate and referendum laws.

Publicity Department, Shanghai Special Municipal Party Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party

Local Correspondence

Kunshan

Kidnapped Child Fortunately Rescued: Duan Guan, the son of Tao Bohe, who resides in Zhongtao Lane, South Street, was taken out to play by his cook, Sun A'guan, at 3:00 PM on the 21st. Unexpectedly, he had not returned by 8:00 PM that evening. The family was alarmed and worried about other possibilities, so they reported to the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team for investigation. Captain Wang dispatched detectives to investigate and temporarily detained A'guan's wife, Sheng, and his friend, Ni A'lin. There was no news that night. At 8:00 AM on the 22nd, Sun A'guan suddenly returned to Kunshan by rickshaw with Duan Guan. The detectives arrested Sun and notified the Tao family to take the child home. Captain Wang interrogated Sun A'guan. According to him, yesterday he took the young master (Duan Guan) out to play on the street. Suddenly, two people came, pulled out pistols, and threatened him to follow them. He had no choice but to follow them to the Luxiabang Station and then take a train to Shanghai. Fortunately, he met a friend named "Little Tiger" at the Shanghai station, who dispersed the two men. He then sent him to the Baodai Society on Sanma Road for the night, and returned to Kunshan this morning. Captain Wang, finding the story inconsistent, submitted it to the General Bureau for county-level interrogation.

Third District Clearing of Public Property: The county's Third District is formed by the organization of the old Anting and Luxiabang townships. It has 1,000 mu of public property land, most of which is held by individuals. After the former District Chief Yang took office, he began to clear it up. However, because the town head of Huajiaqiao and others wanted to compete for it as township property, he resigned repeatedly and had not fully recovered it. It was resolved at the eighth district affairs meeting to continue the previous method and order the township heads to investigate and report. It is also reported that more than 20 town heads of Anting and others have jointly submitted a petition to the county government and the Department of Civil Affairs requesting a thorough investigation. The Third District Party Department also resolved at the recent general meeting of party members

Page 8

, and submitted a petition to the County Party Department to transfer it to the county government, ordering the Third District Office to thoroughly investigate the matter.

Qingpu

Major Opium Case Cracked: Chen Pansheng, a native of this county, has no legitimate business. The other night, he was carrying a package and wanted to leave the North Gate by steamboat. However, because of his flustered appearance, he aroused the suspicion of the gate guard, who ordered him to put it down for inspection. Sixty packets of opium were found, and he was immediately taken to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the county government for interrogation. The suspect, knowing that the赃物 were all there, could not deny it and confessed to trafficking opium. The judge, in view of the strict prohibition orders, dared to smuggle a large amount of opium, which was extremely illegal, sentenced him to three years and six months in prison and fined him 3,000 yuan. If he is unable to pay, he will be allowed to offset each three yuan with one day of imprisonment.

Wujiang

Pingwang Seizes Rice Boat Leaving the Border: The former Rice Inspection Station of Pingwang District in this county, located at the intersection of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, seized a rice boat leaving the border from the Yuanfengtai Rice Shop in Pingwang Town, carrying more than 70 shi of brown rice. It was immediately sent to the county, where the judge interrogated him. He confessed to transporting it to Shanghai for sale, but denied transporting it to Zhejiang Province.

Zhejiang Water Police Come to Town to Arrest Bandits: Xu Pucheng, the head of the Second District of the Zhejiang Water Police, under the secret order of Hang Yi, the commander-in-chief of the Jiahu Bandit Suppression, took a warship to Xiaodongmen within this city and arrested Li Zhonghua, the head of the gang. He was taken aboard the warship that day and sent to the Jiaxing Command Headquarters for interrogation.

The Provincial Government Appoints Two More County Magistrates: Zheng Chengyuan, the former magistrate of Liyang County, was dismissed for owing a large sum of money. Recently, the provincial government appointed Yuan Guanying, a section member of the Finance Department, to succeed him. In addition, Xia Yueqing, the magistrate of Qidong County, was transferred to the province for further appointment. Zhou Juesheng, the chief of the Sixth Section of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, was appointed to fill the vacant position. The two new county magistrates, Yuan and Zhou, have taken office after receiving their orders.

Huaian Middle School Comes to the Province to Avoid Bandits: Wang Delin, the principal of Jiangsu Provincial Huaian Middle School, recently reported that the bandits in the county were rampant and approaching the county seat, making it difficult to hold classes. Therefore, he led all the faculty, staff, students, and Boy Scouts, totaling more than 170 people, to the province by boat the other day. They are now staying at Zhenjiang Middle School to temporarily avoid the banditry. He also petitioned the Department of Education to transfer it to the provincial government to send troops to aid the county in order to restore the area as soon as possible and avoid wasting their studies.

Another Police School Student Commits Suicide: Graduates of the first undergraduate class of the Police Academy have been assigned to various counties to wait for assignments. There are still many who have not been appointed to positions. In the previous case of the tragic murder of Miao Wencai in Jiangyin, whether it was suicide or murder has not yet been revealed. Tang Gaosong, a student assigned to Taixian County to wait for an assignment, had been waiting in the county for a long time and was appointed as the leader of the police team by the county, but he did not know. Because he was extremely resentful of the world, he suddenly had the idea of ​​dying, so he committed suicide at home, which is very regrettable.

Liyang County Bureau Chief Escorted to the Province: Following reports that Zheng Chengyuan, the magistrate of Liyang County, colluded with Pan Bin, the director of the Finance Bureau, to collect land taxes improperly, citizens, including Di, reported the matter to the provincial departments. After investigation, the provincial government sent officials and police to escort Zheng Chengyuan, Pan Bin, and Shen Zhiqin and Cao Qingzhi, important officials involved in the corruption, to the province for detention. Petition for Relief of Judicial Expenses: The government of Xiyi County also handles judicial affairs, and its expenses are not very sufficient. All kinds of equipment are simple and crude. Since Magistrate Pan took office, he has been shorted 7-800 yuan in two months. He specially drafted two measures to seek relief: (1) Qin Ren would be issued a monthly subsidy of 200 yuan from the fines and requested to be included in the regular expenses and disbursed by the High Court; (2) or this 200 yuan would be allocated from the judicial writing fees to secure funds. If the above two points cannot be approved, the only option is to lay off employees and reduce salaries to suit the specified expenses and avoid compensation.

Jiangyin

County Cleanup Committee Warns Cheng Qing Bao: The County Cleanup Committee issued a warning to the Cheng Qing Bao yesterday (the day of the story), because the newspaper's report of the Jiang Hong case was untrue. The original order stated that after the Jiang case occurred, the society was in turmoil. Those against Jiang gloated and exaggerated the words, using all means to add insult to injury. Those who supported Jiang ran around day and night, trying to deny it. Telegrams and memorials almost made the paper expensive, and the discussions were mixed. The committee is in the process of investigating this case. Although Jiangyin's Shanghai fellow villagers and Cao Jingshan and others have repeatedly defended Jiang Hong and asked to be released on bail, it will not be swayed by any clever words and will seek the truth as the standard for decision-making. At the 26th Weekly Memorial Service for the Premier, Commissioners Gao and Meng reported that they firmly stated that they would not express their attitude on the Jiang case while it was under investigation. The newspaper’s local news column on the 20th of this month stated that the case was部白, and said that the County Cleanup Committee had conducted several investigations and found that it was the same as the situation presented by Jiang Hong, etc., which was extremely mistaken. If it is not an untrue record, it is another intention. Otherwise, what did the rumor catch and what did it say? Such stupidity should not be found in the world of public opinion, let alone in the newspapers guided by the committee. It is very inappropriate. It should have been severely punished to serve as a warning to others and to rectify the public opinion. Considering the first offense, it should be given a serious warning. The editor, Lu Shangquan, was derelict in his duty and should be given a major demerit to observe the effect. If he does not repent, he will be dismissed without pardon.

Township Cleanup Bureau Captures Bandits and Escorts Them to the Province for Interrogation: Tongyi County is conducting township cleanup, starting with bandit areas. Bandits arrested in each district are pre-tried and then escorted to the Provincial Bandit Suppression Command for interrogation. The 31st Rear Hospital is Abolished: The 31st Rear Hospital in Nantong was ordered to be abolished by the General Headquarters. The 480 wounded soldiers currently living in the hospital were transferred to the Rear Hospital in Hangzhou under the command of Deputy Adjutant Rong.

Police Warship Goes to Yancheng to Suppress Bandits: The remnants of Ma Yuren and Shen Guanxi's bandits have not been quelled in the coastal area of ​​Yancheng. The Department of Civil Affairs dispatched the Fuyan police warship to jointly suppress them with the warships of Jia Lu and Hong Ping. They sailed north from the Yunyan River on the 21st. The Fireworks Industry Appeals for Maintaining Livelihood: The fireworks industry in Tongruhai counties has recently been struggling due to the curfew imposed during the bandit suppression, which prohibits the setting off of fireworks. They appealed to the county government to maintain their livelihood. The county government has ordered the districts to handle the matter as appropriate.

Jiangyin

Water Police Inspector Seizes Large Amount of Firearms: Ding Guangqi, Inspector No. 5 of the Second Squadron of the Provincial Public Security Team, inspected ships at Huangtiangang Port yesterday (21st) at 11:00 AM and saw a small sampan with suspicious behavior. Inspector Ding boarded the ship for inspection and found 97 rifles without wooden shells, 8 carbines without wooden shells, and 259 miscellaneous parts in three hidden compartments. The shipowner, Shi Chunsheng (from Yancheng), and the sailors, Sun Zehai and Sun Baishuang (from Funing), were sent to the squadron headquarters for questioning by Squadron Leader Shen Hualong and then sent to the county for handling. It is heard that the firearms were unearthed from the mud in Huangdu and were transported to the Yanfu area of ​​Jiangbei for use by Ma Yuren's troops. The firearms are badly rusted and seem to have been left in the mud, perhaps during the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War. Whether this is true or not remains to be determined by the authorities.

Two Thieves Arrested in Qiancun Robbery Case: Zheng Peizhou, the director of the Ninth Branch of the Wuyi Butou Public Security Bureau, arrested Tao Qinrong, a bandit in the Qiancun robbery case.
