Yixing Fellow Villagers Association Telegram

To the Editors of All Newspapers: Our association, in order to assist with the Xiao case, has appealed to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. We recently sent the following telegram to Minister Wang:

To His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs: Xiao Xin'an, a woman from Yixing, accepted a position as a teacher at the Zhonghua Elementary School on Ambon Island, Dutch East Indies. On August 13th, she departed from Shanghai aboard the "Tjipatti" of the Java-China-Japan Lijn. Tragically, during the voyage, she was subjected to violent assault by the ship's chief officer and second officer, both Dutch nationals. The details have already been reported in various newspapers and need not be elaborated upon. Ms. Xiao traveled thousands of miles alone, crossing vast oceans, to dedicate herself to the education of overseas compatriots. Her character is most admirable. Yet, these two Dutchmen acted audaciously and recklessly, inflicting this humiliation. Human rights are endowed, and national dignity is at stake. All citizens share a deep sense of outrage. Moreover, due to our shared hometown, we find it especially difficult to remain silent. Regarding the matter of Ms. Xiao's humiliation, we earnestly request Your Excellency to lodge a protest with the Dutch Minister to China and engage in serious negotiations until the goal of avenging this egregious wrong is achieved. This would be fortunate for the international community and fortunate for the people of Yixing. Respectfully, the Yixing Fellow Villagers Association.

Unbearable Tragedy: Mother and Daughter Commit Suicide by Hanging Together

Liu Yingzhou is a Social Scourge

He Does Not Treat His Wife and Daughter as Human Beings

Liu Remains Unfazed by the Tragedy

The Authorities Should Impose Severe Punishment

At approximately 7:30 PM last night, a tragic incident occurred at No. 6 Maoxing Lane, Fumin Road, in the southern part of the city. A mother and daughter, abandoned and neglected by the husband/father, committed suicide by hanging themselves together. The details are recorded as follows:

Liu Yingzhou's Transformation

Liu Yingzhou, a native of Dongting Mountain, Suzhou, is 36 years old. He works as an accountant at the Meilun Silk and Satin Store, and his demeanor is that of a refined young gentleman. Fourteen years ago, through a matchmaker, he married the eldest daughter of Zhou Xinfu, a teacher from the same hometown. Mrs. Zhou is the same age as Liu. Initially, they lived in harmony, but before a year had passed, Liu's attitude suddenly changed, and poor Mrs. Zhou was virtually abandoned.

Taking a Concubine in Shanghai: Having decided to abandon his wife, Liu, only three years into his marriage, took a concubine, a woman surnamed Yu (30 years old) from Ningbo, in Shanghai. He rented a separate residence at No. 6 Tanzi Lane, East Street, near the Xiaodongmen, and lived there with her, completely forgetting about Mrs. Zhou. However, Mrs. Zhou had already given birth to a daughter named Yun'e, now 11 years old. Mrs. Zhou originally lived in the countryside of Dongting. Although she had heard that her husband had taken a concubine, as a typical rural woman, she could only endure and accept her fate, hoping that her husband might change his mind.

Living Almost Cut Off: Having found new love, Liu treated Mrs. Zhou as an eyesore. He even took further steps to divorce her. Mrs. Zhou endured what she could, but in the second month of the lunar calendar last year, she took her daughter with her to Shanghai and rented a place on Xundao Street near the Dadongmen. However, Liu still discarded her like worn-out shoes and did not visit her for an entire month. As a result, their livelihood was almost cut off. Fortunately, Mrs. Zhou had a younger brother named Zhou Qifeng, who worked at the Xiexing Chongjin Silk and Satin Factory on Baoding Road in Hongkou, and he provided her with regular assistance.

Attempted Suicide Repeatedly: Until September 21st of last year, Mrs. Zhou and her young daughter Yun'e had attempted suicide by swallowing gold jewelry and matches a total of four times over several months. Each time, they were rescued. On September 21st, through Qifeng's mediation, Liu finally agreed to provide Mrs. Zhou with a monthly allowance of 18 yuan, stipulating that Mrs. Zhou must return to Dongting. Mrs. Zhou then took her daughter back to their hometown. However, the mental anguish she suffered was indescribable.

Pawning Clothes and Jewelry: After Mrs. Zhou returned to Suzhou, Liu did not send her a single penny until March of this year. Forced by circumstances, she again took her daughter to Shanghai and rented a place in the front building of No. 6 Maoxing Lane, Fumin Road. Liu not only did not change his previous behavior, showing no pity for Zhou, but also repeatedly came to pressure her to hand over her clothes and jewelry to be pawned. He was determined to place Mrs. Zhou in an impossible situation, forcing her to return to Dongting. As a result, the tragic incident occurred.

Two Bodies Discovered: The day before yesterday, Mrs. Zhou went to her brother Qifeng's home in Hongkou and poured out her grievances, expressing her disillusionment with the world. After her brother repeatedly advised and comforted her, he sent her home. Yesterday afternoon around 7:00 PM, Qifeng, fearing something might happen, went to visit her in the southern part of the city. Upon entering the room, he found it unusually dark. He could only vaguely see two objects hanging from either side of the bed. He called out repeatedly, but received no response. When he touched them, he realized with horror that they were the bodies of his sister and niece.

Liu was Smoking Opium: Qifeng cried out in shock, and neighbors gathered. By the time they were taken down, both were already dead. Qifeng then went out to report to the police station and searched everywhere for Yingzhou without success. He first went to Liu's father, Liu Ziqing, at Wanlong Shenzhuang, Fuchang Lane, Xiaodongmen, but gained no information. After repeated inquiries, he finally found Liu at Fengji Yanzike, Yangxing Street, in the French Concession. Liu was lying on a couch, smoking opium.

Truly Without Conscience: Qifeng lured Liu to the First District Third Precinct. At this time, Liu seemed to have woken up from a dream. After Chief Jin briefly questioned him, and also summoned neighbor Zhang Ayao to the station to testify, Zhou's suicide note was found on the table. The words were extremely sad and unbearable to read. Looking back at Liu Yingzhou, who had abandoned his wife, he appeared unusually carefree, smiling as if immensely pleased with himself. Alas, this man is truly without conscience. After questioning, Chief Jin ordered the local security to be notified and instructed to report to the court today to request an autopsy.

Why So Many Suicides?

Hidden Worries for Society's Future

May the Authorities Find a Way to Eliminate This

Shi Jianzhang: A young man in Western attire, speaking with a Sichuan accent, arrived at the Oriental Hotel at the intersection of Xizang Road and Sixth Avenue around 5:00 PM on the 19th of this month. He claimed to be named Shi Jianzhang from Sichuan, about 23 or 24 years old. The tea servant led him to Room 246 on the second floor, western section, to rest. Shi went out alone that night and returned around 2:00 AM the next morning. From the night of the 19th until yesterday morning, this was his regular pattern, and the tea servant did not pay much attention. The night before last, after Shi went to sleep, he seemed quite calm. Until this morning, when the sun was high, he had not gotten up. The tea servant knocked on the door around 1:00 PM, and the response was very faint. He asked if he wanted to continue staying, but Shi was lying on the bed, turned to the inside, and a sound came from his throat that was neither yes nor no, with only air and no voice. The tea servant was afraid that the guest had not woken up yet, so he did not dare to make any further noise and left Room 246. About an hour and a half later, the accounting office ordered the tea servant to go and see if he wanted to change rooms. But after entering the room, there was silence, and the guest was lying on the bed, his limbs stiff and in an unnatural pose. Looking at his face, it was purplish-white, and saliva was flowing from the corners of his mouth, as if he was in great pain. The tea servant rushed to report to the accounting office, who in turn notified the Zhabei Police Station to send an ambulance to the Oriental Hotel. Shi was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. It was determined that he had taken a type of opium-based anesthetic. By then, it was already 3:30 PM. Because he had taken too much poison, all attempts to save him were ineffective, and he died in the hospital around 7:00 PM in the evening. All his last words and belongings were taken away by the police station.

Zhang Chunfu: Zhang Chunfu, a 23-year-old native of Ningbo, was a merchant. Yesterday afternoon around 7:00 PM, he checked into Room 165 of the Asia Hotel on Hankou Road. Zhang was wearing a crepe robe and was completely alone, with no belongings. Because he spoke with a Ningbo accent, it was known that he was from Ningbo, but his face was red and flushed all the way to his ears, as if he had drunk too much. Zhang claimed that he was drunk, but his other words were evasive. After entering the room, he did not call for the tea servant. Around 8:00 PM, a moan was suddenly heard from the room, which sounded very painful. The tea servant broke down the door and saw that Zhang's expression was very different, and his breathing was rapid. The tea servant immediately reported to the accounting office, called the police, and hired a car to send him to Renji Hospital for emergency treatment. After receiving the news, the Zhabei Police Station immediately sent detectives to the Asia Hotel to investigate the truth. In the room, Zhang Chunfu's note to his father, Zhang Yinsheng, with the address of No. 351 Anli, Beishan West Road, was found. Another letter was addressed to his father-in-law, Zhou Changhua, generally stating that he was committing suicide due to difficult living conditions and economic pressure.

Chen Yi: Five days ago, on the morning of the 17th, a man and a woman came to the Daxin Hotel on Fuzhou Road and checked in together. The man was wearing a Western suit and claimed to be named Chen Yi from Hangzhou. He used to serve in the military. The woman was also about the same age, with short hair and Western-style shoes, dressed fashionably. They had been staying indoors for several days, with little contact with the outside world. Until 10:00 AM yesterday morning, the two guests had not gotten up. The female servant went into the room to change the bedding and suddenly discovered that both Chen Yi and the woman had been poisoned and were moaning on the bed. The woman's expression was particularly severe. She reported the information to the accounting office, who notified the Zhabei Police Station to send detectives to investigate. The man and woman were immediately sent to Renji Hospital for emergency treatment, and their lives were in danger. Later, a note was found in the room, addressed to the accounting office of the Daxin Hotel, roughly stating that things were unavoidable and that they had unspeakable difficulties.

Ding Jinsheng: Ding Jinsheng, who lived at No. 166 Baoyu Lane, Dongxin Bridge, in the French Concession, was about 30 years old. He had been unemployed for a long time and suddenly felt economically pressured, so he had a rash idea. At 11:30 AM yesterday, he secretly swallowed opium paste. Before long, the poisoning became uncontrollable. His family discovered it and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment, but he died despite the rescue efforts. The hospital then sent the body to Tongren Fuyuantang to await an autopsy.

Lawsuit Over Mother and Son's Property

The French Court Heard the Case Yesterday

The Debate Concluded and Awaits Judgment

Madam Zhou Chen, a widow, retained a lawyer last year to represent her in the French court to sue her rebellious son, Zhou Shu, for squandering family property, requesting that he be declared incompetent to manage his affairs. The court ruled as requested. Afterward, the defendant, Zhou Shu, disagreed with the judgment and presented reasons to request a retrial. The request was granted. After repeated hearings, the court ruled in favor of Zhou Shu. Now, the person against whom the retrial was sought, Zhou Chen, also disagrees with the retrial judgment and has retained lawyers Li Zuyu and Li Xinyang to present new evidence and request a new trial. This was also approved. The court hearing was held yesterday, with Judge Zhu Qisheng presiding over the civil court. The retrial plaintiff's lawyers stated that the retrial request was based on two points. First, regarding the request to restrict capacity, since the retrial court determined that the defendant was not a spendthrift, it ruled that the property at Mintine Lane, etc., should be managed by the defendant. The plaintiff has now discovered that the defendant has sold the property in Jijia Lane and used the proceeds. This point alone proves that the defendant is undoubtedly a spendthrift and can be required to restrict capacity. Second, Zhou Shu is the plaintiff's posthumous son. At the age of fifteen, in 1906 (Guangxu 32), the plaintiff used her private savings to purchase the property at Mintine Lane. At that time, the plaintiff used the name of Zhou Zhongsun and registered it at the law office of Gao Yi. However, Zhou Shu was still young at the time and never went to Gao Yi's office to sign. Now, the plaintiff has borrowed a copy of the Zhou family property division book from the fifth room for inspection, proving that the defendant's grandmother had very little family property when the property was divided. This shows that the property at Mintine Lane was indeed purchased by the plaintiff personally. The defendant's real name is Zhou Shu, also known as Zhou Zhongsheng, not Zhou Zhongsun. There is a letter from his representative lawyer to prove this. It is requested that the retrial be approved. The court replied that the initial judgment should be maintained. The defendant, Zhou Shu, also retained a lawyer to argue that the defendant's real name is Zhou Shu, also known as Zhou Zhongsun. The plaintiff also admitted in the initial statement that Zhou Shu is Zhou Zhongsun. The plaintiff in this case is now requesting a retrial system. This is the beginning of the court's era and should be taken with extra caution. The law must have a certain procedure. The plaintiff's request to restrict capacity is based on the fact that the law only applies to those between the ages of seven and fifteen. As for the Jijia Lane property, it was mortgaged to others due to business fluctuations. How can this be considered wasteful? The second issue is the Mintine Lane property, which was actually purchased by Zhou Shu's grandmother, Madam Ma, with money given to her grandson. Zhou Shu signed it as proof and was not the plaintiff's private savings. Later, due to bad feelings between mother and son, Zhou Chen secretly went to Gao Yi's office to change the name. It is requested that the retrial judgment be executed as before. The plaintiff's lawyer also stated that the defendant sold the Jijia Lane property only after the retrial, which should be restricted. As for the Mintine Lane property, the plaintiff holds the title deed as proof, which clearly shows that the property was purchased solely by Chen. The defendant's lawyer said that it was Zhou Shu's property. Is there any rebuttal evidence presented? In short, the plaintiff is in her twilight years, and her family is alive. If she is wasted by Zhou Shu again, the plaintiff's daughters-in-law and grandchildren will have no one to rely on. He requested a clear investigation. Then, the lawyers of both parties debated for a long time. The court announced that the debate was over and that the decision would be made later.

New Plan for Reorganized Domestic Goods Market

Since its reorganization, the domestic goods market run by Zhang Zilian on Nanjing Road has been working hard to improve its internal decorations. Moreover, in the western part of the market, construction is underway to implement its first declaration, the branch system, to bring together domestic goods from all over the country in one place for the convenience of domestic people's purchases. In addition, it has adopted Ren Jinpin's (Construction Plan for Domestic Goods Business) and is starting to organize (China Domestic Goods Business Joint-Stock Limited Partnership), raising 200,000 yuan to expand its operations. It is heard that Chen Yiting, Wang Hanqiang, Cao Zhigong, and industrial leaders Xiang Songmao, Chen Diexian, Huang Hongjun, Zhang Xianda, Cui Fuzhuang, Tang Shaoqi, Pan Dechun, and dozens of others, who have always been enthusiastic about promoting domestic goods, have participated in the initiation. The plan proposed by Ren focuses on gathering the power of consumers to promote the reorganization of commercial organizations, with the help of the development of agriculture and industry. The entire plan is divided into four stages, and the implementation procedure is divided into stages and listed, which is quite precise.

Daxin Silk and Satin Bureau's Business is Booming

The Daxin Silk and Satin Bureau on Shilu Road in this city is a large silk and satin store that was born to adapt to the new era. Its internal organization is very different from that of old-fashioned stores. The purchase of goods is based on understanding social psychology, drawing patterns, and ordering weaving from various famous factories. It is also heard that it has special agents stationed in France who specialize in collecting new Parisian costume patterns and sending them back for imitation. Therefore, the bureau's various products are able to promote the new and innovate, using the strengths of domestic silk, absorbing the essence of European and Western material civilization, with unique creativity and novel colors, which are extremely popular with customers. Business has been booming in recent days. It is heard that the bureau's new opening low-price period is about to expire. In order to repay the kindness of all circles, it plans to hold an autumn sale at a set time, which will be announced soon.

Robbery on Laotaiping Street Yesterday Morning

Police Officer Chases and Captures a Thief

Later, Two More People Involved Were Apprehended

Yesterday at around 5:00 AM, when an apprentice from the family of Yu Xiangsheng, a local who lived at No. 131 Laotaiping Street and set up a meat stall in the vegetable market, went out to get water, three robbers suddenly broke in. Each took out a pistol, threatening to silence them. They first drove all the people in the store into the back room, where one robber guarded them with a gun. The other two robbers went upstairs to search and loot. After about half an hour, they each fled with the stolen goods. The shop owner chased after them and called for help. The robbers ran from Laotaiping Street, across Zhonghua Road, into Yaojia Lane, and then to Dong Street, intending to flee north. Ha Zhizhu, a police officer from the First District General Office, joined the pursuit. He chased them to the Liujia Lane area under the jurisdiction of the Second Sub-precinct of the First District. Zhou Fuhai, a police officer from Post 31, and Zhao Shucheng, a police officer from Post 36, also joined the assistance. Near Post 32, police officer Wang Zhenbang had already heard the alarm and prepared with his gun. Seeing that there was police blocking his way, one of the robbers raised his pistol and pulled the trigger repeatedly, but the bullet failed to fire. Wang suspected it was a rusted gun, so he bravely raised the gun handle and struck the robber's leg several times, finally knocking him to the ground. At the same time, the police officers chasing from behind had also arrived and captured him. Wang then picked up the gun discarded by the robber and, upon touching the trigger, it suddenly fired with a loud bang, sending a bullet out. Fortunately, no one was injured. After checking the robber's body, they found 100 yuan in paper money, 10 jiao in small coins, 2 diamond buckles, 203 double-hao coins, 47 single-horn coins, one gold bracelet, one child's bracelet, two inlaid gemstone rings, and two pure gold rings, all of which were stolen goods from the Yu family. At the same time, the owner, Yu Xiangsheng, also arrived and stated that, in addition to all the original stolen goods, a phonograph had been discarded by the robber in a nearby trash can and had been picked up by a police officer from the First District. Questioning the captured robber, he gave his name as Jiang Apin, 21 years old, from Ningbo. He used to work at the Pudong Cigarette Factory and currently lives at the home of Lu Sanbao in Lujiazhai, Pudong. He said that the pistol was given to him by Sanbao and that Sanbao instigated the robbery. The night before last, they first met at Room 112, Changfa Machinery Factory in the French Concession, and then went to rob in the morning. According to his confession, Chief Ma ordered Wang Wencai and Tang Mingtao, along with patrol leaders Ma Jie and Cui Xishun from the First District, and police officers Guo Linfu, Ting Lie, Shi Xunwei, Yi Wenlan, Zhang Jitian, etc., to go directly to the home of Lu Sanbao in Lujiazhai, Pudong, and arrest Sanbao. Four yuan in paper money, fourteen yuan in silver dollars, and three photos were found. His wife, Lu Ge's, also had a gold ring. After Chief Ma questioned him severely, he confessed that Jiang Apin and he knew each other. Jiang had committed a crime before and was sentenced to three weeks. His mistress left him because of this, so Jiang suspected that he was having an affair with his mistress, resulting in a deep grudge. Moreover, Jiang sometimes asked him for loans. As for the robbery, he knew nothing about it. When questioned, Lu Ge's confession was the same as Sanbao's. Chief Ma also sent patrol leaders Wang and Ma to Changfa Inn to investigate Miao Caibao, who was related to the case. He currently lives in the back room of the second floor of No. 3, Baxianfang, Baxianqiao, with his mistress, Ms. Chen. Caibao left home shortly after arriving. A photo was found in the room. After Chief Ma clarified the situation, he handed over all the criminals, stolen goods, and evidence to the First District for interrogation. He also submitted a document to the director for verification.

Fudan University Yancheng Fellow Villagers' Concern for Their Hometown

Telegraph to Jiangsu Provincial Government...Requesting Swift Suppression of Bandits

The Yancheng Fellow Villagers Association of Fudan University in Jiangwan, Shanghai, due to the fact that their hometown has suffered from bandits for three months, with the people living in deep water and dire straits, in addition to following the consistent appeals of the Yancheng fellow villagers associations of various universities at sea, yesterday sent a special telegram to Chairman Ye of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and Director Li of the Security Department, making a sincere request to urge them to find a way to completely eliminate the bandits and save the people from their troubles. The words were extremely painful. The original telegram is recorded as follows:

To Chairman Ye of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government and Director Li of the Security Department: Our Yancheng is unfortunate, with disasters coming one after another. After the famine, bandits followed. Houses are in ruins, and the people are suffering. The devastation has spread throughout the entire county, and the number of victims is in the millions. The loyal and righteous land of Song Chancellor Lu Xiufu has been turned into a thistle-filled den of jackals and owls. Those who have personally experienced these tragic situations are heartbroken, and even those who see it with their own eyes cannot help but shed tears. The Shanghai newspapers have no reporters to disclose the actual situation of the suffering in Yancheng, and the troops stationed in the area are too weak to resist the stubborn bandits. Moreover, reports to the superiors say that Ma Ni has fled east or that the area has been cleared. In fact, bandits are still everywhere in the countryside. The people of Yancheng are weeping silently and living in deep water, unable to escape their plight for even a day. Recently, Shagou Town was looted and burned, destroying more than 100 houses and shooting more than 20 townspeople. 136 men and women were abducted. Zhao Yusheng, a well-known and upright gentleman, was kidnapped by bandits and killed by stray bullets. The heartbreaking scene is horrifying, and those who hear it change color. Alas, what crime have the people of Yancheng committed? Our association members are concerned about their hometown and feel the pain deeply. We urgently express our words, our hearts are broken. We humbly request that the officials of our provincial government have compassion and do their best to thoroughly suppress the bandits and address both the symptoms and the root causes, so as to completely eliminate them and save the people from their troubles. This would be fortunate for the people of Yancheng and fortunate for the country. Respectfully, the Yancheng Fellow Villagers Association of Fudan University.

Illegal Imprisonment of Wife Case Awaits Sentencing

Li Tan Found to Have No Illness

Li Kebin, a Guangxi native residing at No. 826, Pingliang Road, was discovered by Yangshupu Police Station No. 2160, Section Head Xiang Jianchun, to have illegally imprisoned his wife, Ms. Tan, in the pavilion building between the 9th and 13th of this month, locking the door and depriving her of food. He reported this to the police station, who, together with Chinese and Western detectives, went to rescue Ms. Tan, sent her to the hospital for treatment, and took Li Kebin to the Special District Court. According to Li, Ms. Tan's mental illness had recurred recently, and she wanted to beat people from time to time, so the runaway nanny locked her in the room, denying the allegations of food deprivation. He was ordered to be remanded in custody, and Ms. Tan was sent to the hospital for examination. The details have been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday, Judge Ge Zhitan continued the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. Attorney Zhang Tianyin of the police station stated the case and stated that Li Zhou, the defendant's concubine, was at home during the adjournment and had asked the defendant's nephew, Li Shiyan, to write a letter to a Mr. Lin, asking him to come to court to testify that Li Tan had a mental illness. The letter was discovered by the Chinese and Western detectives who went to investigate, so Ms. Zhou was arrested and detained in the women's prison, and now included in the defendant's position. However, Ms. Tan was also sent to the hospital by the police station and was found by the doctor to have no illness, and the words she said in the hospital were also coherent. The letter and inspection form were presented to the court for inspection. Li Tan spoke in Guangxi dialect, and a woman from the same province translated. At first, she refused to speak, and frequently looked at the two defendants, as if she was afraid of them. Judge Ge understood the situation and ordered the police to take the two defendants out of the courtroom and keep them separate. According to Li Tan, she came to Shanghai with her husband, Li Kebin, from their hometown. Her husband married Li Zhou as a concubine three years ago. Recently, she and the concubine, Zhou, had been in disharmony. She had been locked in the pavilion building for about three days and did not know who had ordered it, but she had been given food. She also stated that she had a daughter in Guangxi, and her other statements were not very clear. According to Li Shiyan, the defendant, Li Kebin, is his uncle. He came to Shanghai with him last year and is currently studying at a school. He lives in the school and only goes home on Sundays. He did not know anything about his aunt, Li Tan, being imprisoned. The letter presented in the case was written by Li Zhou. Li Tan used to scold people, but he did not know anything else. Judge Ge ordered the police to bring the two defendants before the court. Under questioning, they firmly denied the allegations of Li Tan being deprived of food. Li Kebin firmly stated that Tan had been locked in the room because she was sick and that he had ordered it, and that the concubine, Zhou, had nothing to do with it. He begged for leniency. Judge Ge verified the statements, appointed a lawyer to defend the two defendants, and then ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody and scheduled to be sentenced at a later date.

Yang Heshang's Fate Uncertain

Elder Brother-in-law Pursues Child Support Payments

Yang Panicked and Helpless, Leaves a Note and Flees

Yang Heshang, a resident of Pudong, is thirty-eight years old and lives at No. 192 Dongyangjiazhai in Pudong. He currently works as a clerk at the Yonghe Customs Brokerage near the Tianhougong Bridge, earning a meager income. Yang lost both parents at a young age and has one younger brother. He was raised by his grandmother since childhood. At the age of seventeen, he married a woman surnamed Zhu from a nearby village through a matchmaker. After three years, she gave birth to a son. However, she fell ill after childbirth and soon passed away, leaving behind a son named Zhifu. At the urging of his mother-in-law, the child was entrusted to Yang's elder brother-in-law, Kang Jinbao, to raise. After losing his wife, Yang's appetite waned, and he became despondent. His mother-in-law, taking pity on him, arranged for him to marry a woman surnamed Yu. They lived together for three years without having any children, and then Yu also fell ill and passed away. His mother-in-law's love for her son-in-law did not diminish, and two years later, she arranged for Yang to marry a woman surnamed Fan, who bore him a daughter, now ten years old. Yang's son, Zhifu, was raised by the Kang family and is now nineteen years old, working at the Fuhe Customs Brokerage on Second Avenue. Kang has already arranged a marriage for him, but Zhifu is in love with another woman, and their affection is deep. Both parties desire to marry. When Kang learned of this, he was furious and forced Yang to sign an agreement to take his son back, severing the foster relationship, and demanding repayment of the past child support expenses. Yang was shocked and panicked upon hearing this. The thought of fleeing arose spontaneously. On the 26th day of last month, at seven o'clock in the morning, after breakfast, he left without saying where he was going, went straight to his sister's house, took out a key and a letter from his sleeve, handed them to his sister to keep, bid a final farewell, gave some instructions, and left Shanghai with tears in his eyes. His sister was unable to stop him and sent the key and letter to his wife. After reading the contents, she knew that there was no way to bring him back. She could not determine whether Yang would commit suicide after leaving or if he was still alive. As he has not returned for several days, she fears the worst. Yesterday, his wife, Fan, sought assistance from various agencies to find him. Although Yang's letter is not well-written, it is extremely tragic. It is transcribed below: "Yang Heshang, my life is truly bitter. My mother died at three, my father at seven. My grandmother raised me. Later, at seventeen, I married. My wife and I worked to make a living. Within three years, a son was born. His mother became ill and died in two days. Later, my mother-in-law, surnamed Zhu, advised Kang Jinbao to take Zhifu. Yang Heshang is now unsettled and wanders outside. Later, I married a woman surnamed Yu. We both worked to make a living, but I had no money to support my son. Unexpectedly, after two or three years, Yu also passed away. Because of my bad luck, I wandered outside. After wandering for a year or two, my mother-in-law, surnamed Zhu, had a good heart and, seeing her poor son-in-law wandering outside, arranged for me to marry a woman surnamed Fan. After we married, Zhifu was betrothed without notifying Yang Heshang. You intentionally didn't return my son, and you didn't inform me about the important matter of betrothal. My son is indulging in pleasure outside and not doing proper work. I didn't take him back in the past two or three years because you wouldn't let me without money. This matter is lost. Kang Jinbao and my son intentionally ruined things. Therefore, starting from July 30th this year, Kang Jinbao forced me, Yang Heshang, to sign an agreement. I, Yang Heshang, knew that my son was wandering outside, so I refused to sign the agreement. He forced me to sign it on August 21st. After signing, Yang Heshang felt suffocated and unhappy. In case of any untoward event, please discuss it, Fan Liugen, Yang Ruihua." (Note: Fan is Yang's maternal uncle, Yang Ruihua is Yang's older brother.)

Free Talk

A Word or Two

— Wei

A woman's heart is like kindling. Heat it, and it's as soft as cotton, clinging and inseparable; cool it, and it's as hard as stone, shattering at the touch.

It's easy to get a young girl for a wife, but hard to turn a woman into a companion.

Predicting three years from now, a young lady going out without a Western-suited man will be bizarre news.

Girls around ten years old already know how to flaunt their charms.

Don't allow the word "difficult" to exist in your heart when doing things, and don't allow the word "easy" to exist in your heart when studying.

When borrowing money from someone, you fear not seeing them; when the repayment date approaches, you fear seeing them.

If a woman invites you to go out, escape as quickly as possible if you can, otherwise you're doomed.

A woman's tears are like sweet dew, but also like poison, able to revive someone with a drop, but also able to kill someone with a drop.

Watching a fire on the street makes one feel that the Chinese people are still capable of something. If all schools throughout the country posted rejections of love letters, the post office's annual income would decrease by at least hundreds of thousands.

Foreigners see the map of their own country as a fertile and beautiful garden; Chinese people see the map of their own country as a worthless lithographed piece of paper.

Most people are more enthusiastic about reading advertisements for new movies in the newspaper than reading special dispatches about the recapture of Zhengzhou.

An Evening Conversation with an Officer of the Punitive Expedition

— Lü Bing

Since the rebellion of Yan and Feng, the Central Government has launched a punitive expedition. Several months have passed, and the war is about to end completely. The various armies on the front lines have successively reported victories and are returning in triumph. The Double Tenth Festival is being celebrated in addition to National Day. This can be regarded as a good sign for the future of the country. The Pukou Railway Station has been filled with the footsteps of triumphant troops in recent days. My friend, Tang Jun Ji'an, who serves in the military, has also come to the capital amidst the cheers of welcome, his clothes still covered in dust from the journey. He trimmed the candle and talked with me about the battle situation in Bian and Zheng. I will record his words to share with readers.

Feng's ambition was to defend to the death, aiming to fortify his walls and entrench his defenses to exhaust our troops. The trenches he built in Lanfeng were built based on the mountains for protection, spanning tens of feet in width and reaching several fathoms in depth, winding like dragons and snakes, arranged in layers, and mutually reinforcing each other. When the Central Army advanced fiercely, the morale of the Feng army wavered, and they retreated step by step. Liu Zhi, Chen Tiaoyuan, and others thoroughly inspected the Feng army's positions after the victory and praised the completeness of the fortifications. They noted that such trenches were rarely seen in recent wars in our country. However, although Feng was good at defending, the Central Army was even better at attacking. With the determination to sacrifice for the cause, they finally broke through his strong trenches in the final battle. The Central Army is known for its fighting prowess. In addition to the Training Division, Feng's army deeply feared the division of Jiang Guangnai. Feng's subordinates repeatedly encountered Jiang's division and would say to each other, "Here come those fellows again!" The meaning of their words reflected a deep admiration for Jiang's division's perseverance and unwavering courage. The soldiers of Jiang's division were mostly from Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, and Guizhou, and their repeated battles across several provinces left no opponent unscathed.

When Zhengzhou was under the control of Feng's army, at the outbreak of war, the residents were trapped in a dangerous city, living in constant fear. Central aircraft occasionally launched attacks, and the rebel army could not avoid them. They dug holes everywhere to avoid the targets. Many residents also lived in these holes, which were quite spacious, with front and rear entrances for entry and exit, and which could be opened and closed. To alleviate the stuffiness of long-term living underground, they installed pipes to provide ventilation. This underground life was no different from a dark hell. When bombs fell, landslides and cave-ins would occur, leading to live burials. Such tragedies were common. It was not until the Central Army drove straight in and established control that the city emerged from the darkness and saw the light of day again.

The Rich Beggar

— Qiushui

The two characters "(beggar)" make us think of "(no money)." It is only because they have no money that people become beggars. People who are beggars will never be rich. However, in reality, while rich people will certainly not beg from door to door, those who beg from door to door are not necessarily poor. Recently, I have heard two very interesting stories from friends and from Western newspapers. I will write them out to prove that what I say is not a fallacy.

Chinese Beggar Woman Commands Servants. The first story takes place locally. In a lane in the Shanghai Concession, a certain family surnamed Mou rented a two-story residence. There were no men in the household, only a mother and daughter, and they employed a nanny. The nanny, surnamed Wang, was from Ningbo. The person telling the story knew her well. According to the nanny, when she first came to work for the Mou family, she was surprised by the mother and daughter's sleeping during the day and going out at night. She constantly paid attention to their actions. The mother and daughter lived very extravagantly. Their food and living arrangements were very particular. They always got up in the afternoon around 2 or 3 o'clock. Around 5 or 6 o'clock, they would leave in a hurry, carrying bundles of clothes. They would not return until midnight. After returning, the nanny often saw the mother and daughter taking out copper coins and silver from their pockets, countless in number. The nanny became increasingly suspicious. One night, she decided to follow them. She lost track of them midway. Helpless, she wandered the streets to see what would happen. After walking for a long time, she reached the side of a large company on Nanjing Road. Suddenly, she saw a female beggar behind her, begging relentlessly. The nanny turned around and was shocked to see that it was her mistress. The female beggar, seeing that the person walking was her nanny, turned red with shame and left without saying a word. The next day, the mistress confessed everything and discussed it with the nanny, asking her to keep it a secret and promising her a higher salary. The matter was settled. A beggar woman renting a Western-style house and commanding servants is truly an odd thing.

Foreign Beggar with Car and Western-Style House. The second story is a foreign one and is even more interesting. According to recent reports, a man in Liverpool, England, recently committed suicide in his residence. He left behind a "confession" stating that he was a beggar by profession and had profited handsomely for ten years. He earned at least several shillings a day and owned a small Western-style house. He went out early and returned late, wandering the streets to do business that required no capital and little effort. The foreign beggar lived even more comfortably than the Chinese beggar woman mentioned above. This man, named Hanson, was only thirty-six years old when he died. The reason for his suicide remains a mystery. At the same time, there is another beggar in Liverpool who, according to Mr. Brass, the director of the inquiry department of the British Charity Association, earns 600 to 700 pounds a year. He owns a Western-style house and even has a car for recreation! He is a beggar by day and a gentleman by night. His life is more comfortable than that of anyone else. Mr. Brass also said that there is a young man in the same place who has received a commercial education. Initially, he was unemployed and his family was poor, so he pretended to be a victim of the European War. He used his eloquent pen to write letters to wealthy people, asking for assistance. The results were surprisingly good. From then on, he stopped seeking legitimate employment and hired two secretaries to write and mail such begging letters everywhere. His annual income was very high. He can also be considered a beggar with a novel approach.

Strange Tale of a Cat Painting Catching a Mouse

— Dong Ji

A friend came from Zhejiang Province and told me that there was a certain Jia Yizhen in Ningbo who was good at painting, especially birds and animals. He sat alone in his room all day long, washing brushes, practicing paper, admiring ancient styles, and mixing colors. He did nothing else. One day, after finishing dinner, he casually painted a cat and placed it on his desk. That night, a mouse came to the desk in search of food and suddenly saw the cat, baring its fangs and claws, vividly lifelike. The mouse was greatly frightened and turned to flee, but it slipped and fell into the spittoon. It couldn't jump out and drowned. Alas, the mouse's death was not due to the spittoon, but indirectly to the cat painting catching it. Even Sima Yi of the Three Kingdoms, known for his wisdom and courage, lost his nerve at the sight of a wooden statue, let alone a mouse. I record this.

Talking About Drum Singing

— Lao Can

There are now several styles of drum singing: Beijing Drum Singing, Fengtian Drum Singing, Shandong Drum Singing (also known as Pear Blossom Drum Singing), and Beijing-East Drum Singing (also known as Guest Drum Singing). All are named after places and have strong regional characteristics. However, Plum Blossom Drum Singing incorporates various tunes and is the most progressive. It resembles the new Tianjin tunes. Octagonal Drum is a specialty of the Manchus, originating from the victory songs of the Banner troops and not belonging to the drum singing category.

Pear Blossom Drum Singing is the oldest. "Pear Blossom" was originally called "Plowshare Shard," a piece of broken iron from a farm implement. Farmers sang agricultural songs, using broken and discarded farm implements, echoing the ancient practice of striking the earth and hitting wood. This shard was later specially made by ironworkers, and now it is mostly made of copper, gradually losing its original form. Pear Blossom Drum Singers are all from Shandong and sing full-length suites. Now, women mostly sing excerpts.

Beijing Drum Singing emerged with Liu Baoquan and Bai Yunpeng, and was then called Drum Singing. It emphasizes diction, uses vocals well, adds gestures and expressions, and follows drama closely. The rhythm uses flexible beats, breaking free from traditional patterns. It imitates the expressions and voices of characters in books vividly, so the singing is vivid, colorful, emotional, and reasonable. The beauty of the sound is unmatched. Singing "Ning Wu Pass," "Battle of Changsha," "Huarong Road," etc. (Gao Ting Company has records), is like a living dragon and a fierce tiger, making people's eyebrows dance and their faces flush. It is truly an exquisite skill. Bai Yunpeng's spirit is not substantial, so he is only suitable for stories of flowers and moonlight.

Regarding talent in Pear Blossom Drum Singing, "The Travels of Lao Can" praises Bai Niang. Those I have seen, such as Li Yuping and Li Da Wang, can be called masters. Some may dislike Pear Blossom Drum Singing for being too rustic, but its charm lies in this. The Shandong flavor and color are all in Pear Blossom Drum Singing. It must be heard.

Among the talent in Octagonal Drum, Chang Shutian and He Zhichen are outstanding. Those with elegant lyrics include "Returning Boat in Wind and Rain," and those with humorous lyrics include "Five Saints Ascend to Heaven" and "Cui Ping Mountain." "Five Saints Ascend to Heaven" has wonderfully beautiful lyrics that inspire imagination. I particularly enjoy listening to it.

Silver Screen News: Pei Si Kai Deng is known in the film industry as the king of cold-faced comedy. His previous films, such as "Sports Doctor," "Small Boat Owner," and "The Final Victory," were all sensations. The film "Pleasant and Leisurely," recently shown at Carlton, has also received excellent reviews. He recently starred in another film, "Flowers Fall, Water Flows." Not only are the jokes novel and abundant, but there are also several scenes, such as a lonely boat capsizing in the sea amidst alarming waves, Deng flipping over a sail blown into the air by a gale, and, when the ship catches fire, risking his life to rescue the beauty, and fighting fiercely with bandits at the bow of the ship, repeatedly being thrown into the ocean, which are all extremely thrilling. The plot is also tortuous and bizarre, attracting people's attention. The film will be released at the Paris Grand Theatre on the 23rd of this month (Thursday). (Xin Fu)

Roman Art Observation Notes (3)

— Wang Yachen

The murals in Roman churches are all famous works by previous great painters. We should pay special attention to them when studying art. The murals in St. Peter's and St. Paul's Cathedrals are all made of stone inlays. This cathedral has dozens of religious paintings inlaid with Raphael's drafts. The precision of its craftsmanship can be compared with the paintings of the Renaissance.

Speaking of the cathedral's architectural items, there is quite a history. There are three most famous cathedral domes in the world, namely London's Cathedral, Paris's Pantheon, and Rome's St. Peter's Cathedral. This cathedral dome was built by Michelangelo and is most valuable in architectural history.

Beneath the copper pavilion in the cathedral is the tomb of St. Peter. A platform is built in front of the tomb, with an open space in the center. Visitors can look down and see the tomb door. The platform is surrounded by more than a hundred oil lamps, lit all year round. Before Napoleon, they were made of pure gold. When Napoleon dominated Europe, he took the gold lamps. What exists now is of copper, only its style is ancient. Beside the copper pavilion, there is a bronze statue of St. Peter. According to the translator, this statue existed three hundred years before Peter was born. It is actually a famous Greek sculpture. Later, Peter's face was replaced. Those who do not know this mistakenly believe it to be from Peter's time. Believers must touch the toes of the statue. Now half of one left toe has been worn away. Touching the toe is just a superstition.

(1) The Pantheon Pabtgeon, Pantheon is the largest kind of construction. It can be translated as "Shrine of Saints and Sages" because the tombs of ancient celebrities are placed inside. What can be specially recorded here is the tomb of the great painter Raphael. There are many tombs of Roman popes placed in the shrine. Raphael was a painter, but he was also buried here with the royal family. It can be seen that the Romans of that time valued artists.

Raphael Rophael (1462-1520) was invited to Rome by the Roman Pope in 1508 to create the murals in the Sistine Chapel. He was the most favored by the Pope. His style was popular and pleasing, expressing a kind of love that made people feel intoxicated. Although he had a short life of only thirty-seven years, he left behind many magnificent achievements.

Warmth in the Heart (299)

— Bao Tianxiao

Episode 15: Tears of Sadness on All Sides, Yearning for Red Love, A Room Captivated, Lingering Green Intentions

Because of economic factors, families often become abnormal. Like the young master of the Yin family, he leans towards his mother's side, but only for the reason of asking his father for money. The first thing he will ask is your purpose. If your purpose is not correct, he will reject it. But there are many purposes that are inconvenient to disclose. The young master is somewhat dissatisfied with this. He says that if financial matters are to be made public, then they should all be made public. When it comes to unclear purposes, how often does his father report the purpose of the funds he spends? For this question, a country can often erupt in parliamentary impeachment and public complaint, and the Minister of Finance is so frightened that he dares not attend. Large families often have this kind of drama. The young master Yin wants to please his mother, so he spies on his father's actions. When he discovers some facts, he reports them to his mother and asks for a reward. At first, he was only helping his mother, but later, he became a spy to obtain rewards, even fabricating and embellishing the facts. One day, Mrs. Yin obtained a statement from the coachman Geng Sheng and discussed it with her advisor, the young master, saying, "I already used Geng Sheng to pretend to have done something meritorious. He said that the master lives in a small house on the bend of Baker Road. Where do you think Baker Road turns?" The young master said, "With these five words, 'Baker Road turns,' it will be easy to find. The first thing a detective needs is a clue. With a clue, you can use it to find it. I have now read several volumes of Sherlock Holmes' detective stories and have made great progress in detective science. I guarantee that I will find the master's small house by tomorrow morning. When the master is not at home, we can help you deal with him. What do you think?" "But tonight, I bought something that cost two hundred dollars. It's too much trouble to go to the accounting office to get it. Will you pay me?" Mrs. Yin scolded, "You little devil, you're taking advantage of the situation to extort me again. You just took one hundred and forty dollars last month. What did you use it for? Now you're asking for even more." The young master said, "It's not like that. I bought a gramophone and sent it home so everyone can listen to it. It saves us from running out at night. We can just listen to the gramophone every night, and it will pass the time." Mrs. Yin thought, "That's right. If we buy a gramophone, everyone can listen to it. This money can be accounted for in the future. Now that we are at war, it's reasonable for children to like to buy some toys." So, she gave him two hundred dollars and said, "Since you boast of your detective skills, tell me the address and street number of the master's small house tomorrow morning after you find it." The young master took the two hundred dollars, but he certainly didn't buy a gramophone. He probably sent it to some house. But having received the right, he cannot neglect the obligation. The detective work must be done.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Market Shows Signs of Improvement Again

Changes Occur Constantly. Yesterday, the 22nd, the gold price showed signs of recovery. The weighted average price broke through the 70 tael mark. However, instability was inherent during this period. When there was a trend to rise, the total fluctuation in the front and back markets was more than four taels. Foreign exchange seemed to be showing a profit. Banks mostly sold. Dealers tended to climb into the market. The buying and selling prices of various firms were very different. From the front market, Yuan Mao Yong, Yu Da Hua, Tai Wan Xing, Shun He, and those engaged in arbitrage trading bought considerably, and retail investors almost certainly covered their short positions. However, Heng Xing, Yuan Cheng, Yong Yi Feng, Yong, and others all sold. Market sentiment turned firm again. Although overseas silver markets rose, they still lacked upward momentum. Silver prices did not move, and exchange rates continued to rise. Thus, the gold price was initially flat. Afterwards, buyers became active, and the trend was diligent, gradually rising. Although exchange banks sold, the price never relented. By almost noon, it had exceeded 72 taels. However, there was an occasional fluctuation of one or two taels. Later, there were no large-volume transactions in the back market, and since it was Wednesday, the exchange market was weak, with only a little more than one tael of fluctuation. The final stable price was calculated at 72 taels and a fraction. As for silver bars, there were rumors of a downward trend.

The Initial Flatness is Followed by a Winning Streak. The opening price for December gold was 569.6 taels, only down 0.1 taels from the previous day's closing price (the gross price was between 71 taels and under 70 taels). This was because British silver bars only rose by 1/16, and New York silver prices did not change. Furthermore, the British-Japanese spread was plus 1/32, and the US-Canadian spread was plus 1/16. Therefore, market sentiment was still stable, but Heng Xing had already sold, immediately causing a drop to 69.1 taels. Soon after, Yu Da Hua, Tai Tai Heng, Yuan Zhi Feng, Yong, and others competed, causing a jump of one tael. Then, exchange rates followed closely, and the Dalian gang pushed the market up strongly. However, the banks suddenly became firm and raised prices. Banque Belge sold November gold at 1.27 taels, and Korea bought it at 1.26875 taels. Until the first clearing house announcement, it was 72 taels. The listed price did not move, and then rose again to 73 taels. Yuan Xing Yong and Heng Xing Yuan also bought. Soon after, due to a scramble for premiums and sales by Zhi Feng Yong Heng Xing, and sales of December British gold at 173.75 and November gold at 31.25 by banks like the British and Banque Belge, it fell by more than two taels and ten points to 70.03 taels. After a while, retail investors came to buy, raising it by one tael and ten points, and then by one tael and six cents. Banks were willing to sell British gold. Banque Belge continued to sell December gold at 173.75. Also, banks like Hua Bank and American-Japanese banks mutually traded. Citibank December gold traded at $39.25. Banque Belge and Mitsui also sold recent Dalian gold at 1.273125 taels. Banque Belge also sold January British gold at 174.375. As a result, gold prices turned downstream, and arbitrageurs took the opportunity to sell, breaking the 70 tael mark, at 11 o'clock, to 69.78 taels. Afterwards, Wan Xing Shun Li Da De Cheng and speculators came to buy. Moreover, since demand was strong and sellers were hesitant, there was a jump of more than three taels, trending sharply upward, reaching 73.5 taels near the close. After a while, it was 3.2 taels. The closing price did a small fraction, calculated as 2.45 to 2.8 taels, after which Yuan Mao Yong and others sold. The published price was still 618.6 taels, calculated to be pressed down by 45 to 6 taels.

The Market Calmly Settles Down. The after-market opened at 73.3 taels (gross price from 2.67 taels to more than 3 taels). Due to rumors that the Indian exchange rate had contracted by four annas, Yong Feng and others sold, reducing it by 6 or 7 cents, to 72.67 taels. Then, retail investors came in, reaching 73.34 taels after 2:15. Afterwards, it hovered around 3 taels. By 2:20, it had reduced its gains at the close, and the price was extremely flat, holding steady at around 73 taels for about half an hour. Around 3:30, Yi Feng Yong Yu Da and others tended to unload, causing a drop of more than one tael, to 71.7 taels at 3:45. Because the foreign exchange market was closed on Wednesday, retail investors immediately sought to buy, raising it by 5 or 6 cents, to around 72.3 taels around 4 o'clock. It rose and fell by 3 or 4 cents afterwards, and Yu Da sold quite a bit. At the closing bell at 4:30, it was calculated at 72.2 taels, and the closing price was up 2.5 taels compared to the previous day. The highest price for the day was 73.5 taels and the lowest price was 69.1 taels, a difference of 4.4 taels. The listed price was calculated at 46 or 47 taels. Interest Rates Still Fall Back

Market Overview. The foreign market situation seemed to be still stable during the past week. Although there were slight fluctuations, the results were generally similar. However, in the middle of this week, it suddenly sought lower prices. Although there were no sudden bursts, it was generally a decline. As for the trend of the money supply, current demand is indeed not weak. However, the silver reserves are flooded, and there is no way to arrange them. Furthermore, with the crowding of long-term loans coming due, it is even more impossible to arrange them. In the end, it is heading towards a path of easing.

Interest Rates (Foreign Interest). The morning rate was 7 cents, 2.5 mills, 6 haos, and 2.5 hus, weaker by 1 hao and 2.5 hus than the low price in the afternoon market of the previous day. Due to scarce transactions and weak competition in the afternoon market, the resulting market price was the same as in the morning market. (Silver discount) The morning rate only opened at 4%, and the afternoon rate was 5%, slightly weaker by one or two points than the previous day. There were no listed prices or additional water from banks.

Continued Record of Long-Term News

Recently, silver and money businesses have been moving forward bravely and making every effort to carry out long-term transactions. Yesterday, it was heard that both the northern and southern timber industries were initiating transactions, but both sides were holding their ground and had not yet concluded a deal. In the financial sector, the majority of the interest rates set by this gang in April were 8 taels and 2.5 cents. Since the rollover of this period cannot be increased slightly, the minimum should be the same as before (i.e., 8 taels and 2.5 cents). In the timber industry, it is generally said that from this autumn to the present, the war in Fujian Province has spread and the source of timber has been cut off, and the silver funds are useless, only consuming interest. Moreover, according to the general trend, it may be difficult to recover temporarily in these six months, and there is no hope of recovery. Instead of wasting silver interest in vain, it would be better to repay the long-term loans that are due. If it is necessary to roll over the loans, the interest rate should be slightly lower than the previous term, so that the burden can be slightly reduced. According to their tone, the highest interest rate they are willing to pay is only 8 taels, otherwise they will prepare to repay the loans. As a result of this difference of 2.5 cents, each party has held its ground based on their reasons, and the result has not yet been concluded. As far as one can see, it is feared that the financial sector will find it difficult to win, and most of them will not exceed 8 taels. Also, the miscellaneous grain, soybean, and rice gangs are also unwilling to continue to roll over their loans because the rice market has collapsed and business has become difficult. Most of them intend to repay, so most of them have not yet been decided. However, a small number have already made a deal, with prices around 10 taels, but large transactions have not been finalized, and this small number cannot be used as a standard.

Flour Market Hovers with Slight Upswing

Yesterday, the flour market generally showed a hovering trend for each month. At the beginning of this month, the sentiment was slightly fatigued due to the floating of more returns. Afterwards, the attitude of the major manufacturers was slightly tighter. The deliveries in the future should be scarcer than in the previous months. Also, since the inventory is not abundant, it is feared that it will not be possible to reach the 3-cent mark again. November was also tired at the beginning, but then followed the rising trend. As for December, due to the excessive backwardation, the market situation was particularly rising. The rest were all stable. Looking at the later steps, it seems that the foreign goods set by small factories cannot arrive immediately. The future is still looking good once sales become active. As a result, this month did not move, November was good by 0.25 mills, December was good by 0.2 cents, January was good by 0.75 mills, and February and March did not move.

Piece Goods Market Prices Remain Firm

Yesterday, the local cotton market saw fine cloth prices increase slightly, by two and a half to five fen.

Yesterday, two to three hundred pieces of 16-pound goods were sold, causing prices to rise across the board. Yang He, Blue Double Fish, Wen Tai, and Ningbo goods continued to be purchased, so prices remained firm. Prices for both Eastern and Western piece goods remained firm. Eastern goods, especially various types of serge, are almost depleted. Goods that were difficult to sell last spring are now unusually popular. Ma Yan serge sold for 2 qian and 6 fen; Luo Wen serge for 2 qian and 7 fen; Da Hui Wen for 2 qian and 6 fen. Recent transactions in English tinplate, driven by increasing purchases from export merchants, suggest the market may be poised for a move. Yesterday, merchants from Tianjin, Qingdao, and Niuzhuang bought a total of seven to eight hundred boxes of goods. The price was 13 taels and 7.5 qian per box for 90-pound tinplate and 14 taels and 7.5 qian for 100-pound tinplate. Market inventories were found to be very limited, and export merchants were competing to buy, boosting confidence and pushing prices higher. According to those familiar with the situation, once business with the Jing Han Kou store picks up, the market outlook is sure to improve.

Youth Garden

Law School Legal Research Association Held a Lecture Yesterday

Regarding the past history and work situation of the Law School Legal Research Association, this journal has published articles from time to time and there is no need to repeat them. We now know that the Association held its first lecture in the seventh classroom at 4 pm yesterday (according to this association, it is one of the special committees affiliated with the Legal Research Association). Ms. Jin Guangmei served as the chairman, and more than 30 members attended the meeting. Many other students also came to listen. First, the chairman made a brief opening statement, and then the lecture began, in the order of the topics submitted in advance: (1) Mr. Wang Jijin spoke on "How to fundamentally eradicate bandits and communists"; (2) Mr. He Qingyuan spoke on "Law and Time"; (3) Mr. Huang Guocui spoke on "The Development and Changes of Social Concepts"; (4) Mr. Deng Moujia spoke on "Will the Second World War occur in the Pacific?" The grand theories lasted for two hours. Because of the time, there were still several members who had submitted topics in advance, but there was no time for lectures, so they had to wait until next week. Although the atmosphere in the venue was still quiet and the listeners were still full of energy, at six o'clock, everyone inevitably felt hungry. Helpless, the chairman announced the adjournment of the meeting. The chairman's closing remarks at that time can also be called a preview. An excerpt is as follows:

(Although there are still a few people who haven’t spoken, time does not allow it, so we have to leave it to the next session. Of course, we should deeply express our apologies to these students. But at the same time, it is also extremely gratifying. We have achieved such results today, and everyone is so energetic. This sincerity in being enthusiastic about the association is fully expressed, which is truly gratifying. Here, I must report one thing to everyone: we have been locked in this room for so long, and we have been listening to some emotionless social sciences. Of course, exchanging knowledge and practicing eloquence are equally important, and you should not be tired of it. However, social science is fundamentally rational. In other words, what we talk about and listen to is purely rational, lacking emotion, too serious and not a little playful. This is like eating a stomach full of food without being able to digest it. I think you may be feeling too bloated. I intend to do some conditioning work and make coffee and tea after dinner to help you digest. Because everyone has to prepare very good social science materials every time, I might as well change the air and adjust the taste to increase everyone's interest. I think it's okay to talk about other issues, even love issues, social issues, co-education issues, the issue of lovers and friends, etc. We don't care whether they are valuable or not, just to adjust our tastes. I don't know what you think. If you think there are any points that can be adopted, then I can be responsible for this task, and please convey it to other members who are not here today.)

After the speech, there was a lot of applause, which must have been welcomed by the listeners. It is expected that at the second lecture, members will be even more enthusiastic, and the grand occasion will be sincere. (Yi De)

Jinan University Hires a New American Lecturer

The School of Business at Jinan University recently hired Dr. C. F. Rmere, a professor from the University of Michigan in the United States, as a special lecturer. Dr. Lei came to China from the United States to specialize in studying the commercial situation in our country. At the same time, he was hired by Jinan University to give a lecture once every two weeks. The topics discussed are quite valuable. The topics are listed below:

(1) The Relationship between Modern Economic Development and Politics

(2) The Recent Economic Status of the United States Internationally

(3) The German Reparations Issue

(4) The Impact of Silver Price Decline on China's Foreign Trade

(5) A Study of Foreign Investment in China

(6) An Explanation of the Balance of International Trade

It is now reported that Dr. Lei is scheduled to give his first lecture starting on the 16th. His speech will definitely have a performance and value. (Lu)

Recently, the products have been particularly improved, and the prices are low, making them extremely popular among people around the world. The factory has sent a large batch of new goods, such as two-color pens with pearlescent colors for 20.08 yuan each, and sapphire, amber, and gold-black colors for 18.20 yuan each. Forever warranty pens are available in emerald green, sapphire, pearlescent, orange, black, redwood, green, and gold-black colors, which are extremely beautiful, ranging from 11.85 yuan to 34.75 yuan each. Forever warranty mechanical pencils range from 7.80 yuan to 11 yuan each. Ordinary fountain pens are 6.87 yuan to 15 yuan each, and ordinary mechanical pencils are 2.60 yuan to 7.20 yuan each. The latest style of desk pen holders is 59.50 yuan each, and purchasing a pen holder allows for six types of usage. Other items such as marble pen holders range from a little over 20 yuan to 185.75 yuan each. A large number of spare parts are also readily available, such as new parts that can be reconfigured for broken nibs, and the prices are also low.
